       The `[1m$[0m' character introduces parameter expansion, command  substitution,[m
       or  arithmetic  expansion.   The parameter name or symbol to be expanded[m
       may be enclosed in braces, which are optional but serve to  protect  the[m
       variable  to  be expanded from characters immediately following it which[m
       could be interpreted as part of the name.[m
[m
       When braces are used, the matching ending brace is the first `[1m}[0m' not es‚Äê[m
       caped by a backslash or within a quoted string, and not within an embed‚Äê[m
       ded arithmetic expansion, command substitution, or parameter expansion.[m
[m

[14;1H       mands read from the standard input or from a file.  [1mBash[0m  also  incorpo‚Äê[m

[17;1H...skipping...
   [1m[7mPathname[27m[0m[7m [27m[1m[7mExpansion[27m[0m[m
       After word splitting, unless the [1m-f[0m option has been set, [1mbash[0m scans each[m
       word for the characters [1m*[0m, [1m?[0m, and [1m[[0m.  If one  of  these  characters  ap‚Äê[m
       pears,  and  is  not quoted, then the word is regarded as a [4mpattern[24m, and[m
       replaced with an alphabetically sorted list of  filenames  matching  the[m
       pattern  (see  [1mPattern[0m  [1mMatching[0m  below).   If no matching filenames are[m
       found, and the shell option [1mnullglob[0m is not enabled, the  word  is  left[m
       unchanged.  If the [1mnullglob[0m option is set, and no matches are found, the[m
       word is removed.  If the [1mfailglob[0m shell option is set,  and  no  matches[m
       are  found, an error message is printed and the command is not executed.[m
       If the shell option [1mnocaseglob[0m is enabled, the match is performed  with‚Äê[m
       out  regard  to the case of alphabetic characters.  Note that when using[m
       range expressions like [a-z] (see below), letters of the other case  may[m
       be  included, depending on the setting of [1mLC_COLLATE.[0m  When a pattern is[m
       used for pathname expansion, the character [1m``.''[0m  at the start of a name[m
       or  immediately following a slash must be matched explicitly, unless the[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 2028 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       shell option [1mdotglob[0m is set.  In order to match the filenames [1m``.''[0m  and[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 2029 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       [1m``..''[0m, the pattern must begin with ``.'' (for example, ``.?''), even if[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 2030 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       [1mdotglob[0m is set.  If the [1mglobskipdots[0m shell option is enabled, the  file‚Äê[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 2031 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       names  [1m``.''[0m   and [1m``..''[0m  are never matched, even if the pattern begins[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 2032 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       with a [1m``.''[0m.  When not matching pathnames, the [1m``.''[0m  character is  not[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 2033 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       treated  specially.   When matching a pathname, the slash character must[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 2034 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       always be matched explicitly by a slash in the  pattern,  but  in  other[m

[13;1H       [1mBash[0m is an [1msh[0m-compatible command language interpreter that executes com‚Äê[m
[14;1H       mands read from the standard input or from a file.  [1mBash[0m  also  incorpo‚Äê[m
[15;1H       rates useful features from the [4mKorn[24m and [4mC[24m shells ([1mksh[0m and [1mcsh[0m).[m
[16;1H[m
[17;1H       [1mBash[0m  is  intended  to  be  a conformant implementation of the Shell and[m
[18;1H       Utilities  portion  of  the  IEEE  POSIX  specification  (IEEE  Standard[m
[19;1H       1003.1).  [1mBash[0m can be configured to be POSIX-conformant by default.[m

   [1m[7mBrace[27m[0m[7m [27m[1m[7mExpansion[27m[0m[m
       [4mBrace[24m  [4mexpansion[24m is a mechanism by which arbitrary strings may be gener‚Äê[m
       ated.  This mechanism is similar to [4mpathname[24m [4mexpansion[24m,  but  the  file‚Äê[m
       names  generated need not exist.  Patterns to be brace expanded take the[m
       form of an optional [4mpreamble[24m, followed by either a series of comma-sepa‚Äê[m
       rated  strings  or  a sequence expression between a pair of braces, fol‚Äê[m
       lowed by an optional [4mpostscript[24m.   The  preamble  is  prefixed  to  each[m
       string  contained within the braces, and the postscript is then appended[m
       to each resulting string, expanding left to right.[m
[m
       Brace expansions may be nested.  The results of each expanded string are[m
       not  sorted;  left  to right order is preserved.  For example, a[1m{[0md,c,b[1m}[0me[m
       expands into `ade ace abe'.[m
[m
       A sequence expression takes the form [1m{[0m[4mx[24m[1m..[0m[4my[24m[1m[..[0m[4mincr[24m[1m]}[0m, where [4mx[24m and  [4my[24m  are[m
       either  integers  or single letters, and [4mincr[24m, an optional increment, is[m
       an integer.  When integers are supplied, the expression expands to  each[m
       number  between  [4mx[24m  and [4my[24m, inclusive.  Supplied integers may be prefixed[m
       with [4m0[24m to force each term to have the same width.  When either  [4mx[24m  or  [4my[24m[m
       begins  with  a zero, the shell attempts to force all generated terms to[m

[7m Manual page bash(1) byte 117130 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       letters  are  supplied, the expression expands to each character lexico‚Äê[m

       [1m[7mArithmetic[27m[0m[7m [27m[1m[7mExpansion[27m[0m below).  Word splitting and pathname expansion are not[m
       performed.   Assignment  statements  may  also  appear  as arguments to the[m
       [1malias[0m, [1mdeclare[0m, [1mtypeset[0m, [1mexport[0m, [1mreadonly[0m, and [1mlocal[0m builtin commands ([4mdec‚Äê[24m[m
       [4mlaration[24m  commands).   When  in  [4mposix[24m [4mmode[24m, these builtins may appear in a[m
       command after one or more instances of the [1mcommand[0m builtin and retain these[m
       assignment statement properties.[m
[m
       In  the  context  where  an  assignment statement is assigning a value to a[m
       shell variable or array index, the += operator can be used to append to  or[m
       add  to  the variable's previous value.  This includes arguments to builtin[m
       commands such as [1mdeclare[0m that  accept  assignment  statements  ([4mdeclaration[24m[m
       commands).   When  += is applied to a variable for which the [1minteger[0m attri‚Äê[m
       bute has been set, [4mvalue[24m is evaluated as an arithmetic expression and added[m
       to  the  variable's current value, which is also evaluated.  When += is ap‚Äê[m
       plied to an array variable using compound assignment  (see  [1mArrays[0m  below),[m
       the  variable's  value is not unset (as it is when using =), and new values[m
       are appended to the array beginning at one greater than the array's maximum[m
       index (for indexed arrays) or added as additional key-value pairs in an as‚Äê[m
       sociative array.  When applied to a string-valued variable,  [4mvalue[24m  is  ex‚Äê[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 682 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K...skipping...
   [1m[7mArithmetic[27m[0m[7m [27m[1m[7mExpansion[27m[0m[m
       Arithmetic expansion allows the evaluation of an arithmetic expression  and[m
       the substitution of the result.  The format for arithmetic expansion is:[m
[m
              [1m$(([0m[4mexpression[24m[1m))[0m[m
[m
       The  old format [1m$[[0m[4mexpression[24m[1m][0m is deprecated and will be removed in upcoming[m
       versions of bash.[m
[m
       The [4mexpression[24m undergoes the same expansions as if it  were  within  double[m
       quotes, but double quote characters in [4mexpression[24m are not treated specially[m
       and are removed.  All tokens in the expression undergo parameter and  vari‚Äê[m
       able  expansion,  command  substitution,  and quote removal.  The result is[m
       treated as the arithmetic expression to be  evaluated.   Arithmetic  expan‚Äê[m
       sions may be nested.[m
[m
       The  evaluation  is  performed  according  to  the rules listed below under[m
       [1mARITHMETIC[0m [1mEVALUATION[0m.  If [4mexpression[24m is invalid, [1mbash[0m prints a message in‚Äê[m
       dicating failure and no substitution occurs.[m

[20;1H       [4mProcess[24m  [4msubstitution[24m  allows a process's input or output to be referred to[m
       using a filename.  It takes the form of [1m<([0m[4mlist[24m[1m)[0m or  [1m>([0m[4mlist[24m[1m)[0m.   The  process[m

       of  the  expansion.   If the [1m>([0m[4mlist[24m[1m)[0m form is used, writing to the file will[m
       provide input for [4mlist[24m.  If the [1m<([0m[4mlist[24m[1m)[0m form is used, the file passed as an[m

       is supported on systems that support named pipes  ([4mFIFOs[24m)  or  the  [1m/dev/fd[0m[m
       method of naming open files.[m

       When  available,  process substitution is performed simultaneously with pa‚Äê[m
       rameter and variable expansion, command substitution, and arithmetic expan‚Äê[m
       sion.[m

[1m[7mARITHMETIC[27m[0m[7m [27m[1m[7mEVALUATION[27m[0m[m
       The shell allows arithmetic expressions to be evaluated, under certain cir‚Äê[m
       cumstances  (see the [1mlet[0m and [1mdeclare[0m builtin commands, the [1m(([0m compound com‚Äê[m
       mand, and [1mArithmetic[0m [1mExpansion[0m).  Evaluation is done in  fixed-width  inte‚Äê[m
       gers  with  no  check  for  overflow,  though  division by 0 is trapped and[m
       flagged as an error.  The operators and  their  precedence,  associativity,[m
       and values are the same as in the C language.  The following list of opera‚Äê[m
       tors is grouped into levels of equal-precedence operators.  The levels  are[m
       listed in order of decreasing precedence.[m
[m
       [4mid[24m[1m++[0m [4mid[24m[1m--[0m[m
              variable post-increment and post-decrement[m
       [1m-[0m [1m+[0m    unary minus and plus[m
       [1m++[0m[4mid[24m [1m--[0m[4mid[24m[m
              variable pre-increment and pre-decrement[m
       [1m![0m [1m~[0m    logical and bitwise negation[m
       [1m**[0m     exponentiation[m
       [1m*[0m [1m/[0m [1m%[0m  multiplication, division, remainder[m
       [1m+[0m [1m-[0m    addition, subtraction[m

[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mBash[0m  is  an  [1msh[0m-compatible command language interpreter that executes com‚Äê[m
       mands read from the standard input or from a file.  [1mBash[0m also  incorporates[m
       useful features from the [4mKorn[24m and [4mC[24m shells ([1mksh[0m and [1mcsh[0m).[m
[m
       [1mBash[0m  is intended to be a conformant implementation of the Shell and Utili‚Äê[m
       ties portion of the IEEE POSIX specification (IEEE Standard 1003.1).   [1mBash[0m[m
       can be configured to be POSIX-conformant by default.[m

       [1m[7mEXPANSION[27m[0m section.[m
[m
       When [1mbash[0m is invoked as an interactive login shell, or as a non-interactive[m
       shell  with  the  [1m--login[0m option, it first reads and executes commands from[m
       the file [4m/etc/profile[24m, if that file exists.  After reading  that  file,  it[m
       looks  for  [4m~/.bash_profile[24m,  [4m~/.bash_login[24m, and [4m~/.profile[24m, in that order,[m
       and reads and executes commands from the first one that exists and is read‚Äê[m
       able.   The [1m--noprofile[0m option may be used when the shell is started to in‚Äê[m
       hibit this behavior.[m
[m
       When an interactive login shell exits, or a non-interactive login shell ex‚Äê[m
       ecutes  the [1mexit[0m builtin command, [1mbash[0m reads and executes commands from the[m
       file [4m~/.bash_logout[24m, if it exists.[m
[m
       When an interactive shell that is not a login shell is started, [1mbash[0m  reads[m
       and  executes  commands from [4m/etc/bash.bashrc[24m and [4m~/.bashrc[24m, if these files[m
       exist.  This may be inhibited by using the  [1m--norc[0m  option.   The  [1m--rcfile[0m[m
       [4mfile[24m  option will force [1mbash[0m to read and execute commands from [4mfile[24m instead[m
       of [4m/etc/bash.bashrc[24m and [4m~/.bashrc[24m.[m
[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 139 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K...skipping...
       [1m[7mEXPANSION[27m[0m  below),  the  [4mhistory[24m  [4mexpansion[24m  character,  usually [1m![0m, must be[m
       quoted to prevent history expansion.[m
[m
       There are three quoting mechanisms: the [4mescape[24m  [4mcharacter[24m,  single  quotes,[m
       and double quotes.[m
[m
       A  non-quoted backslash ([1m\[0m) is the [4mescape[24m [4mcharacter[24m.  It preserves the lit‚Äê[m
       eral value of the next character that follows, with the exception of  <new‚Äê[m
       line>.   If  a  [1m\[0m<newline>  pair  appears,  and the backslash is not itself[m
       quoted, the [1m\[0m<newline> is treated as a line continuation (that  is,  it  is[m
       removed from the input stream and effectively ignored).[m
[m
       Enclosing  characters  in single quotes preserves the literal value of each[m
       character within the quotes.  A single quote may not occur  between  single[m
       quotes, even when preceded by a backslash.[m
[m
       Enclosing  characters  in  double quotes preserves the literal value of all[m
       characters within the quotes, with the exception of [1m$[0m, [1m`[0m, [1m\[0m, and, when his‚Äê[m
       tory  expansion  is enabled, [1m![0m.  When the shell is in [4mposix[24m [4mmode[24m, the [1m![0m has[m
       no special meaning within double quotes, even when history expansion is en‚Äê[m

       stitution,  arithmetic  expansion, and quote removal (see [1m[7mEXPANSION[27m[0m below).[m
       If the variable has its [1minteger[0m attribute set, then [4mvalue[24m is  evaluated  as[m
       an  arithmetic  expression  even if the $((...)) expansion is not used (see[m
       [1mArithmetic[0m [1mExpansion[0m below).  Word splitting and pathname expansion are not[m
       performed.   Assignment  statements  may  also  appear  as arguments to the[m
       [1malias[0m, [1mdeclare[0m, [1mtypeset[0m, [1mexport[0m, [1mreadonly[0m, and [1mlocal[0m builtin commands ([4mdec‚Äê[24m[m

[m
       In  the  context  where  an  assignment statement is assigning a value to a[m

   [1mSpecial[0m [1mParameters[0m[m
       The shell treats several parameters specially.  These parameters  may  only[m
       be referenced; assignment to them is not allowed.[m
       [1m*[0m      Expands  to  the positional parameters, starting from one.  When the[m
              expansion is not within double quotes, each positional parameter ex‚Äê[m
              pands  to a separate word.  In contexts where it is performed, those[m
              words are subject to further word splitting and pathname  expansion.[m
              When the expansion occurs within double quotes, it expands to a sin‚Äê[m
              gle word with the value of each parameter  separated  by  the  first[m
              character  of the [1mIFS[0m special variable.  That is, "[1m$*[0m" is equivalent[m
              to "[1m$1[0m[4mc[24m[1m$2[0m[4mc[24m[1m...[0m", where [4mc[24m is the first character of the value  of  the[m
              [1mIFS[0m variable.  If [1mIFS[0m is unset, the parameters are separated by spa‚Äê[m
              ces.  If [1mIFS[0m is null, the parameters are joined without  intervening[m
              separators.[m
       [1m@[0m      Expands  to  the  positional parameters, starting from one.  In con‚Äê[m
              texts where word splitting is performed,  this  expands  each  posi‚Äê[m
              tional  parameter  to  a separate word; if not within double quotes,[m
              these words are subject to word splitting.  In contexts  where  word[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 737 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K...skipping...
              enization (see [1mHISTORY[0m [1m[7mEXPANSION[27m[0m below).  The first character is the[m
              [4mhistory[24m  [4mexpansion[24m  character, the character which signals the start[m
              of a history expansion, normally `[1m![0m'.  The second character  is  the[m
              [4mquick[24m [4msubstitution[24m character, which is used as shorthand for re-run‚Äê[m
              ning the previous command entered, substituting one string  for  an‚Äê[m
              other in the command.  The default is `[1m^[0m'.  The optional third char‚Äê[m
              acter is the character which indicates that  the  remainder  of  the[m
              line  is a comment when found as the first character of a word, nor‚Äê[m
              mally `[1m#[0m'.  The history comment character causes  history  substitu‚Äê[m
              tion to be skipped for the remaining words on the line.  It does not[m
              necessarily cause the shell parser to treat the rest of the line  as[m
              a comment.[m

   [1mArrays[0m[m
       [1mBash[0m provides one-dimensional indexed and associative array variables.  Any[m
       variable may be used as an indexed array; the [1mdeclare[0m builtin will  explic‚Äê[m
       itly  declare an array.  There is no maximum limit on the size of an array,[m
       nor any requirement that members be indexed or assigned contiguously.   In‚Äê[m
       dexed  arrays  are  referenced using integers (including arithmetic expres‚Äê[m
       sions) and are zero-based; associative arrays are  referenced  using  arbi‚Äê[m
[7m Manual page bash(1) line 1380 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K...skipping...
       [1m[7mEXPANSION[27m[0m.  When assigning to indexed arrays, if the optional brackets  and[m
       subscript  are  supplied, that index is assigned to; otherwise the index of[m
       the element assigned is the last index assigned to by  the  statement  plus[m
       one.  Indexing starts at zero.[m
[m
       When  assigning to an associative array, the words in a compound assignment[m
       may be either assignment statements, for which the subscript  is  required,[m
       or  a  list  of words that is interpreted as a sequence of alternating keys[m
       and values: [4mname[24m=[1m([0m [4mkey1[24m [4mvalue1[24m [4mkey2[24m [4mvalue2[24m ...[1m)[0m.  These are treated identi‚Äê[m
       cally  to  [4mname[24m=[1m([0m  [[4mkey1[24m]=[4mvalue1[24m [[4mkey2[24m]=[4mvalue2[24m ...[1m)[0m.  The first word in the[m
       list determines how the remaining words are interpreted; all assignments in[m
       a  list must be of the same type.  When using key/value pairs, the keys may[m
       not be missing or empty; a final missing value is treated  like  the  empty[m
       string.[m
[m
       This syntax is also accepted by the [1mdeclare[0m builtin.  Individual array ele‚Äê[m
       ments may be assigned to using the [4mname[24m[[4msubscript[24m]=[4mvalue[24m syntax  introduced[m
       above.   When  assigning  to  an indexed array, if [4mname[24m is subscripted by a[m
       negative number, that number is interpreted as relative to one greater than[m
       the  maximum  index of [4mname[24m, so negative indices count back from the end of[m

[1m[7mEXPANSION[27m[0m[m
       Expansion is performed on the command line after it  has  been  split  into[m
       words.   There  are  seven  kinds  of expansion performed: [4mbrace[24m [4mexpansion[24m,[m
       [4mtilde[24m [4mexpansion[24m, [4mparameter[24m [4mand[24m [4mvariable[24m  [4mexpansion[24m,  [4mcommand[24m  [4msubstitution[24m,[m
       [4marithmetic[24m [4mexpansion[24m, [4mword[24m [4msplitting[24m, and [4mpathname[24m [4mexpansion[24m.[m
[m
       The order of expansions is: brace expansion; tilde expansion, parameter and[m
       variable expansion, arithmetic expansion, and command substitution (done in[m
       a left-to-right fashion); word splitting; and pathname expansion.[m
[m
       On systems that can support it, there is an additional expansion available:[m
       [4mprocess[24m [4msubstitution[24m.  This is performed at the same time as tilde, parame‚Äê[m
       ter, variable, and arithmetic expansion and command substitution.[m
[m
       After these expansions are performed, quote characters present in the orig‚Äê[m
       inal word are removed unless they have been quoted  themselves  ([4mquote[24m  [4mre‚Äê[24m[m
       [4mmoval[24m).[m
[m
       Only  brace  expansion, word splitting, and pathname expansion can increase[m
       the number of words of the expansion; other expansions expand a single word[m

[4;1H   [1mTilde[0m [1mExpansion[0m[m
[5;1H       If a word begins with an unquoted tilde character (`[1m~[0m'), all of the charac‚Äê[m
[6;1H       ters preceding the first unquoted slash (or all characters, if there is  no[m
[7;1H       unquoted  slash)  are considered a [4mtilde-prefix[24m.  If none of the characters[m
[8;1H       in the tilde-prefix are quoted, the characters in the tilde-prefix  follow‚Äê[m
[9;1H       ing  the tilde are treated as a possible [4mlogin[24m [4mname[24m.  If this login name is[m
[10;1H       the null string, the tilde is replaced with the value of the shell  parame‚Äê[m
[11;1H       ter  [1mHOME[0m.   If [1mHOME[0m is unset, the home directory of the user executing the[m
[12;1H       shell is substituted instead.  Otherwise, the tilde-prefix is replaced with[m
[13;1H       the home directory associated with the specified login name.[m
[14;1H[m
[15;1H       If the tilde-prefix is a `~+', the value of the shell variable [1mPWD[0m replaces[m
[16;1H       the tilde-prefix.  If the tilde-prefix is a `~-', the value  of  the  shell[m
[17;1H       variable [1mOLDPWD[0m, if it is set, is substituted.  If the characters following[m
[18;1H       the tilde in the tilde-prefix consist of a number [4mN[24m, optionally prefixed by[m
[19;1H       a `+' or a `-', the tilde-prefix is replaced with the corresponding element[m
[20;1H       from the directory stack, as it would be displayed by the [1mdirs[0m builtin  in‚Äê[m
[21;1H[1;1H       brace expansion with the [1m+B[0m option to the [1mset[0m command  (see  [1mSHELL[0m  [1mBUILTIN[0m[m
[2;1H       [1mCOMMANDS[0m below).[m
[3;1H[m

   [1m[7mArithmetic[27m[0m[7m [27m[1m[7mExpansion[27m[0m[m
       Arithmetic expansion allows the evaluation of an arithmetic expression  and[m
       the substitution of the result.  The format for arithmetic expansion is:[m
[m
              [1m$(([0m[4mexpression[24m[1m))[0m[m
[m
       The  old format [1m$[[0m[4mexpression[24m[1m][0m is deprecated and will be removed in upcoming[m
       versions of bash.[m
[m
       The [4mexpression[24m undergoes the same expansions as if it  were  within  double[m
       quotes, but double quote characters in [4mexpression[24m are not treated specially[m
       and are removed.  All tokens in the expression undergo parameter and  vari‚Äê[m
       able  expansion,  command  substitution,  and quote removal.  The result is[m
       treated as the arithmetic expression to be  evaluated.   Arithmetic  expan‚Äê[m
       sions may be nested.[m
[m
       The  evaluation  is  performed  according  to  the rules listed below under[m
       [1mARITHMETIC[0m [1mEVALUATION[0m.  If [4mexpression[24m is invalid, [1mbash[0m prints a message in‚Äê[m
       dicating failure and no substitution occurs.[m
[m

[19;1H   [1mProcess[0m [1mSubstitution[0m[m
[20;1H       [4mProcess[24m  [4msubstitution[24m  allows a process's input or output to be referred to[m
[21;1H       using a filename.  It takes the form of [1m<([0m[4mlist[24m[1m)[0m or  [1m>([0m[4mlist[24m[1m)[0m.   The  process[m
       [4mlist[24m  is run asynchronously, and its input or output appears as a filename.[m
       This filename is passed as an argument to the current command as the result[m
       of  the  expansion.   If the [1m>([0m[4mlist[24m[1m)[0m form is used, writing to the file will[m
       provide input for [4mlist[24m.  If the [1m<([0m[4mlist[24m[1m)[0m form is used, the file passed as an[m
       argument should be read to obtain the output of [4mlist[24m.  Process substitution[m
       is supported on systems that support named pipes  ([4mFIFOs[24m)  or  the  [1m/dev/fd[0m[m
       method of naming open files.[m
[m
       When  available,  process substitution is performed simultaneously with pa‚Äê[m
       rameter and variable expansion, command substitution, and arithmetic expan‚Äê[m
       sion.[m

[1m[7mARITHMETIC[27m[0m[7m [27m[1m[7mEVALUATION[27m[0m[m
       The shell allows arithmetic expressions to be evaluated, under certain cir‚Äê[m
       cumstances  (see the [1mlet[0m and [1mdeclare[0m builtin commands, the [1m(([0m compound com‚Äê[m
       mand, and [1mArithmetic[0m [1mExpansion[0m).  Evaluation is done in  fixed-width  inte‚Äê[m
       gers  with  no  check  for  overflow,  though  division by 0 is trapped and[m
       flagged as an error.  The operators and  their  precedence,  associativity,[m
       and values are the same as in the C language.  The following list of opera‚Äê[m
       tors is grouped into levels of equal-precedence operators.  The levels  are[m
       listed in order of decreasing precedence.[m
[m
       [4mid[24m[1m++[0m [4mid[24m[1m--[0m[m
